<div id="review_639374734" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/639374734" />
    <a title="Ruth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10008293-ruth"><img alt="Ruth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347534106p2/10008293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/639374734?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruth" href="/user/show/10008293-ruth">Ruth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer639374734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1950358119427014442">Loved this series! Started reading book 1 and couldn't stop until I'd finished book 3. Although these books would be classed as contemporary YA romance, that really doesn't do them justice. Really, they are books about the importance of family, friends, and about growing up and figuring out that life is seldom simple ... The central character, Belly (Isabel), is a fairly typical teenage girl. I liked that she wasn't made out to be some perfect heroine. She was bratty and whiny at times, often co</span>
  <span id="freeText1950358119427014442" style="display:none">Loved this series! Started reading book 1 and couldn't stop until I'd finished book 3. Although these books would be classed as contemporary YA romance, that really doesn't do them justice. Really, they are books about the importance of family, friends, and about growing up and figuring out that life is seldom simple ... The central character, Belly (Isabel), is a fairly typical teenage girl. I liked that she wasn't made out to be some perfect heroine. She was bratty and whiny at times, often confused about what was going on, but clearly a lively and loveable character. The boys ( her brother, Steven, and their childhood friends Jeremiah and Conrad) too were far from perfect; as the series progressed we go to see things first from Jeremiah's point of view and then Conrad's, which added depth to the story, filled in some gaps and also helped to explain various things that Belly herself didn't understand. Their confusion, anger and sadness over various events are well presented, alongside their boyish pranks and banter. The tension between the two brothers, their competitiveness versus their strong brotherly love, is particularly well portrayed. The adult characters are all very 'present' as well, and portrayed in a realistic way. It was good to read a YA story that showed adults as active and concerned, not absent, although one of the themes of the series is the realisation, as the children grow, that their parents are far from perfect. I loved the role played by the beach house, as an anchor point for many of the characters; it almost took on a life of its own. And I enjoyed the way in which the story was told, swapping from present day to flashbacks of the past in a way that seems very natural to me, as current events triggered memories and characters looked back in an effort to find either understanding or comfort. It is not a difficult read, and It only took me a day or so to read all three (!), but it is a story that will stay with me for quite some time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1950358119427014442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307886452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7748551276005961971">I liked the first two books. I hated the third. I absolutely hated it. <br/><br/>Okay, let's set the scene here:<br/> <br/>Belly (or Isabel) grew up around these two dudes. their mom and her mom are bffs and belly feels very close to their mom (Suzannah). belly spends the first book pining over Conrad who is an ass, but also kinda likes her. there's also a subplot surrounding the boy's parents and their marriage and that. okay. so far, so good. <br/><br/>second book, she kinda starts dating Conrad but then he goes AWOL after</span>
  <span id="freeText7748551276005961971" style="display:none">I liked the first two books. I hated the third. I absolutely hated it. <br /><br />Okay, let's set the scene here:<br /> <br />Belly (or Isabel) grew up around these two dudes. their mom and her mom are bffs and belly feels very close to their mom (Suzannah). belly spends the first book pining over Conrad who is an ass, but also kinda likes her. there's also a subplot surrounding the boy's parents and their marriage and that. okay. so far, so good. <br /><br />second book, she kinda starts dating Conrad but then he goes AWOL after a thing happens and that sort of wrecks her relationship with him and she kinda teeters between him and Jeremiah (the other brother). also still kind of a thing happening with their parents. <br /><br />third book, they decide they want to get married while she's still a freshmen in college, and the parents flip out. this is the parents role in this one. they don't get a subplot, they are now the obstacle. we spend way too much time with planning the wedding, which I have never cared about when reading a book. also, the reason they decide to get married is dumb. and she spends most of the first half saying how her current beau is the bomb.com but then the brother shows up and she's all like "which one??! which one??!" all over again.<br /><br />I think the worst part about it is that you feel like Belly lives in a world where these two boys are the only things that matter in life. you sort of hear that she likes swimming and that she's good at it, but when she chooses a college she goes to the same one as her boyfriend. and we don't find out what her major is, I don't think. she doesn't have much in the way of personality, other than "upset" and "in love".<br /> <br />honestly, you could read these. they're readable. but not if you like sustenance. they're basically three books worth of "omg I love them both, they both love me this is a difficult decision" stretched out, and is used as a basis for belly to make important life-altering decisions. <br /><br />just save your money and read some fanfiction. <br /><br />one star, because the author tried.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/8431254-sam">Sam</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8431254-sam?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361498546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18051662739777280252">What makes a good book for me is something that once I start I can't put down-even when my eyes are drooping half shut and it's 2:30AM. I also know's it's left some impact if i'm still laying in bed hours, even days later and i'm still thinking about the book. This series did that to me. 3 times.<br/><br/>Jenny Han did a pretty good job at developing the characters throughout the years. With the series spanning over almost 10 years(and even stories from before then), you got to watch them change and grow </span>
  <span id="freeText18051662739777280252" style="display:none">What makes a good book for me is something that once I start I can't put down-even when my eyes are drooping half shut and it's 2:30AM. I also know's it's left some impact if i'm still laying in bed hours, even days later and i'm still thinking about the book. This series did that to me. 3 times.<br /><br />Jenny Han did a pretty good job at developing the characters throughout the years. With the series spanning over almost 10 years(and even stories from before then), you got to watch them change and grow up. The switching from present to past was a little confusing at first, but it really helped to fill in all the gaps. It gave you a really good background of the story the meaning of all their relationships with one another. You sympathized for all of these characters. Especially when you got to read things from the boy's POV in It's Not Summer Without You and We'll Always Have Summer. They made me want to mourn for their losses, feel saddened for the moments that were missed, and they actually made me laugh out loud in more than a few places. <br /><br />I recommend this series. It's perfect for summer but it's actually not entirely revolved around summer. I'd say only the first one really is. I also recommend you clear your schedule, because you're not going to want to stop until you've finished all 3 of the books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18051662739777280252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1324498875?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aline" href="/user/show/38800534-aline">Aline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141353821" href="/book/show/22317828-the-summer-i-turned-pretty-complete-series">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38800534-aline?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38800534-aline?shelf=love-the-characters">love-the-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38800534-aline?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38800534-aline?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38800534-aline?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38800534-aline?shelf=love-the-cover">love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38800534-aline?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1324498875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16874497282410763307">I just finished it and I'm so emotional right now, with tears and all because it was that good <3 I already convinced my little sister to read this (she reads maybe one book a year). <br/><p>I'm so freaking glad that I picked this series up. I've seen it all over the internet and I've heard only good things about it, but I always judged the book by its title, nahh I don't want to read a book that's named 'The summer I turned pretty', but man was I wrong! I'm glad I've given it a try nontheless.</p><br/><p>It's abou</p></span>
  <span id="freeText16874497282410763307" style="display:none">I just finished it and I'm so emotional right now, with tears and all because it was that good &lt;3 I already convinced my little sister to read this (she reads maybe one book a year). <br /><p>I'm so freaking glad that I picked this series up. I've seen it all over the internet and I've heard only good things about it, but I always judged the book by its title, nahh I don't want to read a book that's named 'The summer I turned pretty', but man was I wrong! I'm glad I've given it a try nontheless.</p><br /><p>It's about family, friendships, first loves, growing up, loss and so much more. If you haven't read this series, do yourself a favour and read it :)</p></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3445595706986532909">Over-all, I think the story is great. Too cliched though, but still, it does made me swoon all over Condrad, and made me all sappy. I loved Susannah so much that when she died, I think if I were one of the characters, I would be more devastated than Con and Jere.   <span id="freeText3445595706986532909" style="display:none">Over-all, I think the story is great. Too cliched though, but still, it does made me swoon all over Condrad, and made me all sappy. I loved Susannah so much that when she died, I think if I were one of the characters, I would be more devastated than Con and Jere. I felt at lost too. <br /><br />The great thing about this book is that when I read it, I felt like I was there at Cousins Beach too. I felt like I was there at the Beach House. I love how Belly always have her late night swims and that ritual they have on their first day in Cousins, the Belly Flop, and all their games like that spin the bottle and everything. Their childhood memories are so beautiful.<br /><br />So it's true! This is what all the girls want. Everything in here: Condrad who is not the flowers-candy type kinda guy but the i'll-give-you-the-moon-and-stars kinda guy (That's my favorite part. You know that Valentine's Day). Jeremiah who is always flippant and always at the middle and is the guy who always puts smiles and laughters on his wake. Steven who is the my-sister-is-a-pain-in-the-ass-but-hurt-her-and-i'll-kill-you kinda brother. And of course, I love the combination of Susannah and Laurel. Susannah's the not too tight kinda mother and Laurel is the opposite to her but I love their friendship. I couldn't put it into words but that's pretty much the friendship I wanna have.<br /><br />I love all the characters in the book but what felt wrong while reading it was Belly. No offense. The name is just too lame. Why can't Isabella be just, Bell or Iz? Or whatever! Belly is just, I don't know... lame? Sometimes, I don't get her. I think she's way too selfish (like for instance, when that fight she had with Taylor. But of course, I understand she's way too young so it's okay to act like that but sometimes, it pissed me. Other times, I liked her. But most of the time, I didn't feel her just like that day on the prom. She should've let Condrad explain first before she rant her stupid hunch that Condrad's gonna end it. I mean if he will eventually break it off, she should at least gave him some time to explain. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong. I like the book. The Belly part was just like my opinion. It's nothing really. I just have to rate it this way 'coz, we all know the story is too cliched but it's still a must read book! Its'like the bright side of life! The setting must have made me feel that way but regardless, it's entrancing!<br /><br />P.S. And oh! Condrad is mine! Bwahahahahaha :D<br /> <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer204771025171448188">Okay so i have a habit of reading a book and half way when i don't see where the story is ending i go to the back and read the last page to get a picture of how it ends so i can be motivated to carry on reading.<br/><br/>When i read The summer i turned pretty and It's not summer without you, i didn't do that i actually read the whole book and didn't skip to the ending. However originally when i read that summer i turned pretty i didn't know it was part of a trilogy i just thought it was one story book. So</span>
  <span id="freeText204771025171448188" style="display:none">Okay so i have a habit of reading a book and half way when i don't see where the story is ending i go to the back and read the last page to get a picture of how it ends so i can be motivated to carry on reading.<br /><br />When i read The summer i turned pretty and It's not summer without you, i didn't do that i actually read the whole book and didn't skip to the ending. However originally when i read that summer i turned pretty i didn't know it was part of a trilogy i just thought it was one story book. So that's why i read without skipping because it was just that good and i wanted to be surprised by the ending. Whe i read the second book i now knew it was a trilogy but i still wanted to read the book naturally. But on the third book i couldn't handle it. The writer strings you along the whole book and the ending is so dramatic in all the books i just couldn't read the book without knowing the ending. <br /><br />In the third book i actually read the last page first, if i hand't done that i would not have read the book at all. and after i read the last page i was heavily motivated to read it and find how Conrad and Belly get married. <br /><br />Overall i think the books are great the last one was the best, from the start i was team Conrad and belly #infinity... <div id="review_214409571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214409571" />
    <a title="Mary Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872215-mary-elizabeth"><img alt="Mary Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600918968p2/5872215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214409571?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Elizabeth" href="/user/show/5872215-mary-elizabeth">Mary Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214409571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15019574162787727762">I read all three books while I was on vacation at the beach, which was cool because the book takes place at one, too. All three were done in two days; simple writing, not a lot of imagination is really needed, and the charters are really cuts and dry: The girl they've known their whole lives turns pretty one summer. Her brother is a jerk, but totally over protective. Jeremiah is the sweet friend, and Conrad, Jeremiah's brother, is the asshole she's loved since she was born. <br/><br/><br/>It's typical.<br/><br/><br/>You can </span>
  <span id="freeText15019574162787727762" style="display:none">I read all three books while I was on vacation at the beach, which was cool because the book takes place at one, too. All three were done in two days; simple writing, not a lot of imagination is really needed, and the charters are really cuts and dry: The girl they've known their whole lives turns pretty one summer. Her brother is a jerk, but totally over protective. Jeremiah is the sweet friend, and Conrad, Jeremiah's brother, is the asshole she's loved since she was born. <br /><br /><br />It's typical.<br /><br /><br />You can probably imagine what happens within three books without actually reading them, BUT, it was kind of nice to be lost in their little perfect world for a couple of days, and I'd rec this book because it was just good. If that makes any sense at all. <br /><br /><br />Do you have some kind to kill and your brain is totally burned out from reading Hate List? Read this then. <br /><br /><br />The author did a good job keeping things easy, she kept true to her characters, and while sometimes it was a little jumpy, I really did enjoy kicking back seaside and reading about Belly and the boys she loves. <br /><br /><br />Until the third book when the author totally did a 360 on the characteristics of the brothers. I might have even given the book five stars, but the third book kind of left me with a "Yeah, right!" kind of feeling. <br /><br /><br />So read it, you'll probably like it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15019574162787727762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UNvQpYJIwABD5+rzkbu08/pkFytbv7fqeX/84/wAMAbpsle4d3/0lvkCzz6Fqb9QGszCiaRemSuhGeLDZk6rGg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2jLGx6IaIVbDicTB9MokVgIhFXFHkcK0jH3EpA89uDVjW0HaVy0VwHls4Qzg2C/14onA07hw7HVUG9qElXMjKQ==')})
  }
//]]>
